Horrible!! Staff has ROTTEN attitude! When I said the Sprite needed more syrup due to tasting off and had more carbon than palatable, she came out, tasted it for herself, and then copped an attitude that it tasted fine to her.  She charged me for a 2nd small soda at regular price. I had bought a sandwich meal deal 1st. Since I didn't want to make a scene, I just paid for it. I HIGHLY recommend avoiding this particular Subway, and I don't usually write bad reviews, but she was so nasty to me!! PS: Interestingly,  after writing this review, the sandwich she made me fell all apart when I opened it to eat it, and the bread crumbled, ALL of it! Eek! Save yourself the time, effort and problems, just DON'T eat here!! I know I never will again!</review>

I just had a moment of nostalgia. I visited this camp 2x's back in the early '90s with my school and had a fantastic experience both times. It just popped in my head, so I looked it up, and the photos brought back some great memories. Night hike, fossil search for sharks teeth, banana slug club, music night, and the list goes. < Text>
I went there for science camp and it could've been better in my opinon. But, let me point out the pros first. The food was good, fresh, and seemed clean. The staff were nice and were really helpful, and had nicknames that made me smile. Now to the cons.
1. The hikes could've been a lot more intresting. It was really just walk, take a break, stop at one place to talk about "nature", and walk back down. It could've been so much more like birdwatching or sightseeing.
2. We had to fill out journals during the one week trip. I get it. They're trying to get us to learn but it really got in the way of trying to enjoy most activites.
3. The cabins weren't very comefortable. They had a shaggy rag to cover a mattress which meant when you sleep it would make an obnoxious sound. And it just felt weird. Plus all of us had to share like two bathrooms.

And that's my overall opinion on science camp! If you're an adult who goes there personally ignore this review. If you're a kid who has went there for science camp I hope we can relate.< /Text>

<Review>I just came back from Mission Springs and had a lovely time. The bathrooms were normal, the showers were spacious, and the cabins were clean. The food was amazing. The naturalists teach you to eat all the food on your plate. The students aim for zero food waste, which is something really fun to do. We hiked a lot, which was a good form of exercise. Of course, we stopped for water breaks, played games that related to the outdoors, did fun activities such as building huts, and learned how to use things like compasses. The last thing I want to point out are the evening activities.You will do things such as campfires and a barn dance. The barn dance is only fun when you really boogie! I had a really fun time. I will miss Mission Springs. It was a once in a lifetime chance and I took it.<//Review><resp>None</resp>< name>

< Text>
My family went on Sunday for the brunch buffet and it wasn't that great but it did have some very good points.  They had chocolate covered strawberries.  GOOD ones.  They had frest fruit like pineapple, watermelon and bananas.  They had a full salad bar with fresh produce and good dressings.  They had 3 soups to choose from (one was their famous Potato Cheese soup).  They had soft and fluffy waffles with warm syrup and butter.  Now, the icky points.  The gravy was too salty, the bacon was paper-thin and completely bland, the made-to-order omelettes were flavorless, the small custard tarts tasted like play-doh, and the sausages were swimming in grease.  Not only was the brunch buffet $15.99 per person but beverages were NOT included so a soda is another $2.79 on top of that.
As we were paying at the front counter and the worker asked me how we enjoyed our meal I told her that it really wasn't worth what they were charging.  She actually asked what had been wrong so I told her.  She apologized and was very kind and sincere and said she'd just started her shift and hadn't looked at the buffet yet.  She was actually the manager and I didn't even catch her name!  She offered to discount our meal which was really nice and not something I expected or was trying to do.  I did tell her that the buffet food just didn't reflect the normal good food we were used to getting there.< /Text>

<user_name>Peggy Fung</user_name>< time>

<Rating>4</Rating>< Text>
4 STAR. Overall. Would return but gotta make sure to specify no MSG otherwise it's just on par with other cantonese restaurants. Love the refillable complimentary free soup though. Not your average cheap free soup. My 7 year old had 2 bowls of that, paired with rice, and called it a meal. Generous portion at an average of $8 to $10 per plate to share. Ordered about one dish per person to share and still have plenty to take home.

Other: On the salty side in general. Some dishes are pre-MSG-ed. Avoid where makes sense. Fast service. Wouldn't be opposed to dine here if chosen by my group of friends. Just double emphasize the no MSG. Newly opened less than a month ago, doing well so far. Let’s hope they keep this up and not deteriorate in quality and portion as is the trend with new Chinese restaurants.< /Text>
